## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: constitutive modeling / thermomechanical materials science
**Analysis**: The task involves predicting stress from strain and temperature, which is a classic constitutive modeling problem in materials science. Temperature typically softens materials by reducing modulus and flow stress, while strain hardening follows power-law or saturating forms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress and power hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear and nonlinear strain response)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress with strain)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (strain hardening with temperature softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1.0 / T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Linear thermal softening with power hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential decrease of flow stress with temperature)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Swift equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal activation)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with cross-coupling)
- Zerilli-Armstrong BCC type: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * T + c3 * T * log(epsilon)) (thermally activated dislocation glide)
- Rational temperature dependence: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1.0 / (c2 + c3 * T)) (inverse temperature softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear decrease of elastic modulus with temperature → multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) on strain terms
- Thermally activated plastic flow → Arrhenius-type exp(c0/T) or exp(-c0*T) multiplicative factors on stress
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) forms indicating dislocation density saturation
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable structure
- Shifted power law for pre-strain → (epsilon + c0)**c1 instead of epsilon**c1 to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Melting/critical temperature behavior → (T_m - T)**c or (1 - c0*T**c1) factors that drive stress to zero at melting
- Logarithmic strain rate sensitivity analog → log(epsilon + c0) terms appearing in quasi-static hardening curves
- Concave-up then concave-down stress-strain → cubic or sigmoidal forms c0*epsilon - c1*epsilon**3 for phase-transforming materials
